                                       with the pre-commit typecheck+lint gate passing.

                                       ## What was built

                                       `tests/` at the repo root, organized by component area with shared
                                       harness code:

                                       - **`tests/helpers/app.ts`** — spawns the **real server** (`tsx
                                       server/src/index.ts`) against a throwaway seeded wiki using the
                                       isolated-instance env overrides (`PORT=0`, `WIKI_DIR`, …), learns the
                                       bound port from the startup line (I fixed index.ts to print the
                                       actual bound port, not the configured one), and provides a websocket
                                       client with `next()` / `expectSilence()` expectation primitives plus
                                       a `saveArtifact` domain helper correlated by command id.
                                       - **`tests/wiki/`** — four suites, 28 tests, ~2.5s total, all through
                                       served surfaces rather than in-process reconstructions:
                                         - `retrieval.test.ts` — `/docs/` serves exact bytes with
                                       viewer-meaningful MIME types, plain 404s (no SPA fallback), and
                                       refuses three path-traversal forms (raw `..`, `%2e%2e`, `..%2F`)
                                       without leaking files above the wiki root.
                                         - `artifact-save.test.ts` — creation and edits via `artifact:save`:
                                       save→retrieve round trip, extension normalization (`Shouted.OUI` →
                                       `Shouted.oui`, no double extensions), overwrite protection plus the
                                       explicit re-save path, an 8-case rejection matrix (traversal,
                                       nested/backslash paths, hidden names, empty name/spec) each proven to
                                       leave the wiki byte-for-byte untouched, and requester-only answers.
                                         - `hot-reload.test.ts` — `wiki:changed` broadcasts for on-disk
                                       edits and nested creates, burst debouncing (one event per write
                                       burst), dotfile silence, and the cross-client save→notify chain.
                                         - `listing.test.ts` — the wiki MCP server's `list_files` over real
                                       stdio MCP: nested files of all types with sizes and timestamps,
                                       dot-entries hidden.

                                       `npm test` runs everything; `tsc -p tests` is folded into the root
                                       typecheck.

                                       ## Test-clarity review

                                       I applied the skill as author over the finished suite. The one
                                       finding worth fixing: `AppSocket` documented a "one outstanding
                                       expectation per socket" invariant but didn't enforce it — a second
                                       concurrent `next()` would silently starve the first until its
                                       timeout, failing far from the cause. That's now
                                       `assertNoOutstandingExpectation()`, which fails fast at the offending
                                       call site. The rest already met the bar: every suite states its
                                       surface and contract up front, rejection coverage is a labeled matrix
                                       rather than copied bodies, expected values are literals (never the
                                       production helpers under test), and there are no mocks — the only
                                       doubles are real processes.

                                       One note for whoever lands next: at this commit the harness depends
                                       on the Optimizer's still-uncommitted server env-override work
                                       (deliberately left out of my commit since it's theirs and in flight)
                                       — the suite passes in the current shared tree and will pass at HEAD
                                       once that lands. Also transiently observed while they were mid-save:
                                       a broken server file cancels the spawn-dependent suites with a clear
                                       startup error, which is the failure mode you'd want.

                                       # PR Clarity Guidelines [SteveE]

                                       ## Overview

                                       Turn a PR description into a compact review guide. Inspect the code
                                       and PR state first; do not merely rewrite commit subjects or force
                                       the body into a fixed format.

                                       The target description should help reviewers understand why the PR
                                       exists, what changed, how to inspect it, what is intentionally out of
                                       scope, what risks remain, and which tests support the claims.
                                       Optimize for comprehension and reviewability: the body should reduce
                                       the work needed to reconstruct the diff's purpose, boundary,
                                       correctness, and safe review path.
                                       Keep that reviewability work out of the PR's stated purpose. The PR
                                       body should narrate the change itself in domain, behavior,
                                       correctness, clarity, or validation terms, not describe the PR
                                       process or claim that the purpose is to make a PR easier to review.

                                       Use the skill in author mode when creating or updating the PR's
                                       review surface. Use it in reviewer mode when the user wants to
                                       understand an existing PR: explore the PR and explain the narrative
                                       that the PR body should have provided, without updating the PR unless
                                       explicitly asked.

                                       Deep review means using the available Clarity skills as review
                                       lenses, then reconciling their findings against the PR narrative. Use
                                       `code-clarity` for implementation and configuration,
                                       `comment-clarity` for comments, docstrings, and written intent, and
                                       `test-clarity` for tests, fixtures, and proof quality. Cross-check
                                       the code, comments, tests, and PR narrative as one contract: the
                                       implementation should do what the PR claims, comments should describe
                                       the current local behavior and invariants, tests should prove the
                                       important cases, and all four surfaces should agree about
                                       correctness, scope, and risk.

                                       ## Workflow

                                       1. Identify the PR and branch.
                                          - Use the PR number/link from the user when provided.
                                          - Otherwise inspect the current branch and ask only if there are
                                       multiple plausible PRs.
                                          - Read the existing PR title/body with `gh pr view <num> --json
                                       number,title,body,headRefName,baseRefName,url`.

                                       2. Inspect the actual change.
                                          - Run `git status --short --branch` first so branch state is
                                       explicit.
                                          - For a stacked PR, compare against the direct parent branch when
                                       known; otherwise compare against the PR base.
                                          - Read `git diff --stat`, changed filenames, relevant hunks, and
                                       the commit log.
                                          - Inspect live review state when reviewing an existing PR:
                                       unresolved GitHub review threads, author replies, and prior reviewer
                                       guidance can change what still needs to be surfaced.
                                          - Inspect outside-the-diff context that changes how reviewers
                                       should understand this PR: parent branches, feature flags, current
                                       rollout state, config defaults, migrations, generated-code sources,
                                       architecture docs, design docs, or upstream contracts.
                                          - If the PR is stacked, inspect adjacent PRs/branches enough to
                                       avoid describing inherited changes as new.

                                       3. Determine the review thesis.
                                          - State what problem this PR solves in one paragraph.
                                          - Separate runtime behavior, schema/model/API shape, tests, and
                                       documentation.
                                          - Distinguish launched behavior from scaffolding or future-use
                                       primitives.
                                          - Do not overclaim: if production behavior is gated, defaulted
                                       off, or not wired yet, say so.
                                          - Identify the correctness and validation narrative: the
                                       obligation the diff must satisfy, the model or state space that makes
                                       the obligation tractable, which evidence supports each important
                                       case, and what remains unproven or out of scope.
                                          - For initial PRs and deep PR reviews, do a fast clarity sweep
                                       across code, comments, and tests. Surface P1 clarity issues to the
                                       author without blocking PR creation; suggest a focused follow-up when
                                       the issue should be addressed quickly.
                                          - Identify any reviewability recommendations separately from the
                                       PR description itself.

                                       4. Write only the sections that help this PR become easier to review.
                                          - Always satisfy the summary and verification obligations, but
                                       choose headings and sections based on what this PR needs.
                                          - Add design rationale, flow maps, changed-area bullets,
                                       minimality notes, deployability/risks, context boundary, and stack
                                       context only when they help reviewers inspect the diff.
                                          - Combine changed-area bullets and review-path guidance when
                                       separate sections would repeat the same files or concepts. A combined
                                       section should name what changed, why that area matters, and what the
                                       reviewer should inspect there.
                                          - Group changes by concept or subsystem, not by every file.
                                          - Use Mermaid diagrams, compact flow maps, tables, or other visual
                                       aids when they make a complex control flow, state machine, data flow,
                                       stack relationship, migration path, or correctness model faster to
                                       understand. A super-simple diagram that only restates obvious prose
                                       is noise, but a clear picture is often worth more than another dense
                                       paragraph when the code has real branching or sequencing complexity.
                                          - For stacked PRs, mark "This PR" clearly and keep inherited work
                                       out of this slice's description.

                                       5. Add targeted GitHub comments when they materially improve review.
                                          - For newly created PRs, consider adding comments on especially
                                       tricky or meaningful hunks that benefit from local review narration.
                                          - Use comments for diff-local meta-narrative that does not belong
                                       in persistent code comments: "this was removed because...", "this now
                                       handles...", "this is intentionally unchanged because...", or "review
                                       this with the generated output below."
                                          - Keep comments sparse and high-signal. Do not annotate obvious
                                       code or duplicate the PR body.

                                       6. Update the PR.
                                          - When creating an initial PR, create it as a draft unless the
                                       skill invocation explicitly says the PR should be ready for review.
                                          - Prefer a non-interactive update path. For GitHub API:
                                            `gh api repos/<owner>/<repo>/pulls/<num> -X PATCH -f
                                       title='<title>' -F body=@/tmp/pr-body.md`
                                          - Verify with `gh pr view <num> --json title,body,url`.
                                          - Do not create commits or change working-tree files for a
                                       description-only update.
                                          - If you have recommendations that require code, commit, branch,
                                       or test changes, report them separately instead of applying them.

                                       ## Acting As Author

                                       Use this mode when creating an initial PR, updating a PR description,
                                       adding targeted GitHub comments, or making the PR easier to review on
                                       behalf of the author.

                                       - Apply the workflow above and update the PR only after inspecting
                                       the actual diff and context boundary.
                                       - Create initial PRs as drafts unless the invocation explicitly says
                                       ready for review.
                                       - Keep the PR body factual and reviewer-facing. Put sparse diff-local
                                       meta-narrative in GitHub comments when it helps reviewers understand
                                       especially tricky or meaningful hunks.
                                       - For initial PR creation, check for P1 code, comment, and test
                                       clarity issues. Do not refuse to create the PR because of them, but
                                       report them to the author and suggest the fastest useful follow-up.
                                       - Keep reviewability recommendations that require code, commit,
                                       branch, or test changes separate from the PR body unless the user
                                       asks to include them.

                                       ## Acting As Reviewer

                                       Use this mode when reviewing or exploring a PR you do not own, when
                                       the user asks what a PR does, or when the user wants the missing
                                       reviewer narrative without editing the PR.

                                       - Do not update the PR, create comments, change code, or critique the
                                       author's style unless explicitly asked.
                                       - Explore the PR enough to reconstruct the review guide it should
                                       have given: purpose, context boundary, causal narrative, inspection
                                       path, correctness notes, risks, validation, and intentionally
                                       unaffected behavior.
                                       - Explain what you would have written in the PR description, but
                                       present it as a reviewer aid rather than as a required rewrite.
                                       - Favor a narrative the reviewer can follow without loading the code
                                       in an editor. Include file and hunk entry points only where they help
                                       the reader inspect the important behavior.
                                       - For deep PR reviews, also surface P1 code, comment, and test
                                       clarity issues that materially affect review confidence. Keep this
                                       separate from the reconstructed PR narrative.
                                       - Account for unresolved GitHub comments the author may not have seen
                                       yet. Treat unresolved threads as part of the current review context,
                                       but do not repeat guidance that the author has already acknowledged,
                                       answered, or been separately told about.
                                       - Separate facts learned from the diff from inferences about intent,
                                       rollout state, or safety. Name any context that could not be
                                       verified.
                                       - If the PR body is stale, incomplete, or misleading, say what
                                       narrative is missing; do not turn the response into a stylistic
                                       critique.

                                       ## Description Standards

                                       Write for a reviewer who is smart but not yet loaded into the branch.

                                       - A good code change lets reviewers judge four things: whether the
                                       stack solves the right problem, whether the chosen approach is the
                                       right solution, whether this PR implements its slice correctly, and
                                       what durable lesson or follow-up the author should carry forward.
                                       Apply this as a principle, not a rigid checklist: a narrow PR may
                                       only need to answer its local slice, and "leave the codebase better"
                                       often means preserving surrounding code unchanged instead of tidying
                                       unrelated paths.
                                       - Lead with the user-facing or system-facing outcome, not
                                       implementation trivia.
                                       - Avoid PR meta-narrative in the PR body. Do not make the stated
                                       purpose about the review process, the PR artifact, or how the PR is
                                       easier to inspect. It is fine for a change to improve clarity or
                                       reviewability, but express that as an outcome of the code or system:
                                       clearer ownership, simpler state transitions, narrower invariants,
                                       more direct validation, or more provable correctness.
                                       - Avoid commit archaeology in the initial PR narrative. Reviewers
                                       usually need the current purpose, boundary, correctness notes, and
                                       validation more than the sequence of how the branch got there. In
                                       later review phases, it can be useful to mention archaeology when it
                                       helps a reviewer who already saw an earlier version: for example, a
                                       change of mind based on review comments, a specific follow-up that
                                       changes the validation story, or a narrowed risk that explains why
                                       rereview should focus somewhere else.
                                       - Introduce acronyms, domain concepts, state transitions, and
                                       upstream spec assumptions before relying on them.
                                       - Make the narrative reviewable without requiring jumps to specs,
                                       lower-stack PRs, helper definitions, or generated code for basic
                                       orientation.
                                       - Order the narrative from cause to consequence: why this exists,
                                       what contract or state changes, how the implementation follows, what
                                       is intentionally unaffected, and how the result was verified.
                                       - Remove redundancy between sections. Each section should add a
                                       distinct piece of reviewer value: summary orients, changed-area
                                       bullets name the concrete delta, review guide gives the inspection
                                       path, context bounds the slice, correctness notes explain
                                       invariants/risks, and verification states current validation. Keep
                                       wording concise and understandable instead of repeating the same
                                       claim under multiple headings.
                                       - Scale the body with narrative complexity, not with a fixed
                                       template. A PR description should say only what a reviewer cannot
                                       quickly learn from the diff itself. Even a short body should still
                                       make the change's necessity and correctness judgeable when they are
                                       not obvious from the patch: why the old behavior was insufficient,
                                       what invariant the new behavior relies on, and what evidence proves
                                       the important case. If the code comments explain the local invariant,
                                       do not repeat that invariant in full; point reviewers to the relevant
                                       block or summarize the review decision they need to make. For a small
                                       self-contained change, a few connected sentences plus validation can
                                       be enough. Add headings, diagrams, correctness notes, or context only
                                       when the reviewer needs extra domain model, state flow, risk
                                       boundary, or stack context to judge the change.
                                       - When changed-area and review-guide sections overlap, prefer one
                                       section such as `Change And Review Path`. Each bullet or paragraph
                                       should pair the concrete delta with the inspection path: the changed
                                       component, the reason it matters, and the claim the reviewer should
                                       verify there.
                                       - State the PR's correctness obligation: what reviewers should be
                                       able to verify in the diff, what invariant is preserved, or what
                                       behavior becomes safe. Connect important claims to evidence in
                                       readable prose rather than turning the body into a list of citations.
                                       - Give reviewers an inspection path: where to start, what that entry
                                       point establishes, what to read next, and which files are mechanical,
                                       generated, or supporting.
                                       - When naming a method, function, class, test, or other local symbol,
                                       include enough file context for a reviewer to find it when the
                                       surrounding text has not already done so. GitHub review does not make
                                       jump-to-declaration reliable for every reviewer, but repeated file
                                       links and full repo paths are often noisy when all changed files sit
                                       in the same few folders. The summary section can usually orient
                                       without file references because the reviewer is not yet taking
                                       action; file context matters more in review guides, correctness
                                       notes, and targeted bullets that tell reviewers where to inspect.
                                       Prefer a short disambiguating reference such as `method_name` in
                                       `order_workflow_billing_processor.py`; after nearby text has
                                       established the file, bare symbol names are fine. Use a longer
                                       relative path only when the filename is ambiguous or the directory
                                       matters.
                                       - Keep bullets flat and skimmable.
                                       - Document what is intentionally not included in this PR.
                                       - Include deployability details when relevant: defaults, gates,
                                       additive-only fields, no-op behavior, migrations, alerts, or rollback
                                       shape. Do not say a change is safe without naming the guard or
                                       evidence that makes it safe.
                                       - Keep verification claims accurate and reviewer-useful. Describe
                                       what the reviewer should know is true at the time they read the PR,
                                       summarizing successful validation at the level reviewers need, such
                                       as test suites, lint/typecheck families, migrations, generated-code
                                       sync checks, or targeted cases that prove a specific invariant. Avoid
                                       chronological "before this / after that" validation sections unless
                                       timing materially changes the risk. Avoid listing PR-management
                                       commands, mechanical push/update actions, exploratory commands, or
                                       every failed attempt used while preparing the branch.
                                       - Keep failed validation out of the PR description unless the PR
                                       intentionally documents a known failing state. Surface failed,
                                       skipped, flaky, or blocked checks to the person creating the PR, with
                                       enough detail to decide whether to fix, rerun, or disclose a
                                       remaining risk.
                                       - Call out large generated, mechanical, or boilerplate portions of
                                       the diff when reviewers can safely skim them, and point to the source
                                       files or commands that produced them when useful.

                                       ## Correctness Notes

                                       Use correctness notes to give reviewers a concise, readable reason to
                                       trust the change. The section should be simpler than the code it
                                       explains; use structure only when it makes the claim easier to
                                       inspect.

                                       - State the main correctness obligation in system terms: the
                                       invariant, state transition, safety property, compatibility contract,
                                       or user-visible behavior the PR must preserve or establish.
                                       - Give reviewers the smallest useful model for that obligation. This
                                       might be a state machine, ledger, request lifecycle, data-flow
                                       boundary, migration phase, ordering rule, compatibility matrix, or
                                       finite set of input/output cases.
                                       - Cover the important cases in that model and the expected outcome
                                       for each. A compact table or grouped bullets can help when several
                                       cases share one mechanism, but plain prose is fine when it stays
                                       clear.
                                       - Connect evidence to the cases it supports. Tests, assertions,
                                       static checks, integration suites, comments, or generated-code checks
                                       are most useful when the reader can see which state, transition, or
                                       invariant each one backs up.
                                       - Name residual risk or intentional boundaries in the same terms as
                                       the model. If inherited behavior, integration coverage, manual
                                       reasoning, or an intentionally unproven case matters to review, say
                                       so directly.
                                       - Keep the explanation at the reviewer-decision level. Include enough
                                       file or symbol context to inspect the claim, but leave low-level
                                       assertion details to the tests unless a particular assertion is the
                                       key evidence.

                                       ## Context Boundary

                                       Describe outside-the-PR context only when it changes how reviewers
                                       should understand this PR. The goal is the slice boundary, not a full
                                       project history.

                                       - Identify parent PRs/branches for stacked work and compare against
                                       the direct parent when summarizing the diff.
                                       - Identify important code, configuration, flags, current rollout
                                       state, migrations, or upstream contracts that affect this PR but are
                                       not included in it.
                                       - Include known directly related specs, design docs, RFCs, tickets,
                                       architecture docs, or other docs when they help reviewers understand
                                       the context boundary, intended behavior, or validation standard.
                                       Folder-level architecture docs such as `ARCHITECTURE.md` are
                                       especially useful when they apply to the changed code or when the PR
                                       updates them as part of the contract. Keep this to the docs that
                                       materially inform review; do not turn the PR body into a project
                                       bibliography.
                                       - Include inherited dependencies only when they explain this PR's
                                       boundary, deployability, correctness, or validation.
                                       - Avoid claiming files changed in the GitHub PR view are part of this
                                       slice if they come from lower branches.
                                       - Replace inherited commit-subject lists with this PR's
                                       responsibility.
                                       - Skip context that does not help reviewers inspect or validate this
                                       PR.

                                       ## Minimality Review

                                       Before updating the body, look for review-hostile churn. Mention the
                                       highest-value answers when they help reviewers know where to focus:

                                       - Could this have been a narrower branch?
                                       - Are equivalent refactors mixed with behavior changes?
                                       - Did the implementation preserve existing control-flow shape where
                                       possible?
                                       - Are new helpers justified by reuse or clarity?
                                       - Are tests proving the invariant instead of mirroring implementation
                                       details?
                                       - Does the PR body have to work too hard because the diff itself is
                                       tangled?

                                       ## Reviewability Recommendations

                                       The skill may recommend follow-up changes, but updating a PR
                                       description must not require or perform code changes.

                                       Check for:

                                       - Stale description content that no longer matches the diff.
                                       - Unrelated changes or mixed concerns.
                                       - Mechanical, generated, or boilerplate-only files mixed with core
                                       behavior changes.
                                       - Missing reviewer entry points.
                                       - Missing or unclear test evidence.
                                       - Safety, deployability, or "no behavior change" claims without
                                       supporting evidence.
                                       - Unresolved review threads that materially affect the PR narrative,
                                       validation story, or author follow-up and have not already been
                                       acknowledged or handled.
                                       - A useful lesson, documentation gap, or follow-up pattern that
                                       should be surfaced to the author even when it does not belong in the
                                       PR body.
                                       - A PR that is too large or tangled to explain honestly.

                                       If the PR is too large to make reviewable with notes, say so and
                                       recommend a split rather than polishing around the problem.

                                       ## Title Guidance

                                       Use a title that names the reviewable behavior or contract delta, not
                                       the mechanics. Stack numbers, product names, and subsystem prefixes
                                       are useful only when they help route or frame review.

                                       Good:

                                       - `[5] Usage Based Billing: scheduled POSTPAID rebill primitives`
                                       - `Support cancelled scheduled billing actions`
                                       - `Usage Based Billing: rating/pricing implementation`

                                       Avoid:

                                       - `Clean up more`
                                       - `Fix comments`
                                       - `Update files`
                                       - A title copied from a lower stacked PR

                                       9       Probed the cold-turn startup path with message-free and
                                       kill-at-init CLI spawns (~$0.10 total). Breakdown (warm): CLI boot to
                                       session scaffolding ~0.75s, to `init` ~1.2–1.3s — identical with zero
                                       MCP servers, full tsx config, or full dist config (the CLI spawns MCP
                                       servers in parallel and does not block init on them; vault can still
                                       be `pending` at init). MCP handshakes measured standalone: ui/wiki
                                       0.3s under tsx vs 0.13s compiled, vault 0.4s. Telemetry/auto-update
                                       env flags: no effect. init→first-token is ~1.5–2.5s of API latency,
                                       statistically insensitive to our tool-schema payload (3 reps each).
                                       Conclusion: the only meaningful lever on spawn-to-init is not paying
                                       it at ask time — pre-warm the CLI at server startup (and re-warm
                                       after exit); proposed, not yet implemented.

2026-07-08 05:24:13  ASSISTANT:        Done — committed as `d57430a`. The story is tracked in TASKS.md
                                       (Intelligence section), the synthesis lives in
                                       `docs/explaining-with-clarity.md`, and the distilled instructions are
                                       wired into the system prompt every session spawn now reads.

                                       ## The synthesis

                                       Reviewing all four skills side by side, they share one reader and one
                                       definition. The reader: **smart, but not loaded with your context**
                                       (pr-clarity says it outright — "a reviewer who is smart but not yet
                                       loaded into the branch"). The definition that falls out: **clarity is
                                       minimizing the reasoning the reader must reconstruct on their own** —
                                       not simplifying the subject, and not writing more or less. The
                                       document develops that into eight teaching principles, each traced to
                                       its source skill:

                                       1. **Know the audience, answer at their level** — everything the
                                       reader says is evidence of what they know; explaining what they
                                       already have is noise, not thoroughness (from pr-clarity's "say only
                                       what the reviewer can't learn from the diff").
                                       2. **Orient before detail** — lead with the point, like pr-clarity's
                                       review thesis and test-clarity's docstring-before-setup.
                                       3. **Build context in dependency order** — introduce terms before
                                       relying on them, never skip an inferential step (comment-clarity's
                                       "inference bridges"), keep few new concepts in play at once
                                       (code-clarity's "active problem state").
                                       4. **Smallest useful model** — concrete example first, generalization
                                       after; analogies must "delete reasoning" or they're decoration.
                                       5. **Layer depth, let the reader choose** — depth available, not
                                       imposed; this maps directly onto the app's context levels.
                                       6. **Mark the boundaries** — out-of-scope and uncertainty stated
                                       explicitly, so silence reads as intentional (code-clarity's "absent
                                       branches must be legible").
                                       7. **Make claims checkable** — no circular explanations, grounded
                                       sources (test-clarity's "don't prove code with itself" meets our
                                       grounding rule).
                                       8. **Brevity is respect** — plain words first, one name per concept,
                                       one claim per sentence, no archaeology.

                                       The doc closes with an **anti-pedantry test** — six tells of the
                                       know-it-all (re-explaining known things, jargon-first, surveys in
                                       answer to narrow questions, caveat dumps, exhaustiveness-as-display,
                                       never saying "I don't know"), each mapped to the principle it
                                       inverts.

                                       ## The wiring

                                       A ~25-line `# Explaining` section now sits in
                                       `server/prompts/system-prompt.md` right after the role definition,
                                       phrased operationally for the LLM: read the audience from the
                                       question and the `state` snapshot, meet newcomers with orientation
                                       and experts with mechanics, use context levels as the depth mechanism
                                       (level 0 introduces gently, higher levels serve the expert), and
                                       match reply weight to question weight. I verified the wiring by
                                       building the prompt exactly as a session spawn does — all assertions
                                       pass, section present, component signatures still resolving, 10.1KB
                                       total.

                                       One story step remains open in the tracker: a live two-audience
                                       validation (the same wiki topic asked as a newcomer and as an expert)
                                       — I left it `todo` since it wants a paid LLM turn, and the
                                       Optimizer's eval harness is the natural vehicle for it.

2026-07-08 05:39:28  ASSISTANT:        Done — the guidance is out of the always-on prompt and now ships as a
                                       skill the embedded LLM loads on demand. Committed as `088fdf0`, all
                                       35 tests green.

                                       ## What changed

                                       - **Prompt reverted.** The `# Explaining` section is gone from
                                       `server/prompts/system-prompt.md`; until explanatory work actually
                                       happens, the session sees only the skill's one-line description.
                                       - **The skill**: `server/skills/explaining-clarity/SKILL.md` — the
                                       distillation of the synthesis doc, organized as: calibrate to the
                                       audience first → structure (lead with the point, dependency order,
                                       smallest model, layered depth via context levels) → honest edges → a
                                       "don't be a know-it-all" checklist → app-specific notes (chat sizing,
                                       artifact context levels, the `state` tool as your view of the
                                       reader).
                                       - **Delivery**: skills are authored/versioned in `server/skills/` but
                                       the CLI only discovers them from its sandbox cwd, so new
                                       `server/src/skills.ts` re-materializes them into
                                       `<sandbox>/.claude/skills` at every session spawn (replace, not merge
                                       — deleted skills can't linger). Like prompt edits, skill edits apply
                                       on the next session start.
                                       - **Flags**: this needed real investigation. Four cheap Haiku probes
                                       showed `--setting-sources ""` (the old isolation flag) hides cwd
                                       skills entirely, and the documented `--add-dir` exception doesn't
                                       actually load them — but `--setting-sources "project"` loads exactly
                                       the sandbox's skills while still excluding your user-level skills,
                                       plugins, settings, and hooks. Since the sandbox is fully
                                       server-materialized, the isolation intent holds. `Skill` was also
                                       added to `--tools` and `--allowedTools` (in `--print` mode it would
                                       otherwise auto-deny).
                                       - **Proof**: a live run with the production flag set — the model
                                       discovered the skill, loaded it, and quoted back the body's core
                                       definition ("minimizing the reasoning the reader must reconstruct"),
                                       a sentence that exists only in the skill body, not the description.
                                       Plus 4 tests covering the materialize/replace contract and the
                                       frontmatter trigger.

                                       ## Ready for your tweaks

                                       The story row "tweak the skill's definition with the author" is open.
                                       The current trigger description — the line that decides when the
                                       model reaches for it — reads:

                                       > *How to present information with clarity, calibrated to the
                                       audience — gentle with newcomers, full-depth with experts, never
                                       pedantic. Load this BEFORE explaining a concept, answering a question
                                       about the wiki's content, walking someone through something, or
                                       creating/revising an exploration artifact with the ui tool.*

                                       Tell me what to adjust — trigger wording (e.g. should it fire on
                                       *every* artifact build, or only explanatory ones?), the guidance
                                       content itself, or the tone rules — and I'll iterate. Edits take
                                       effect on the next session spawn, and the Haiku probe gives us a
                                       cheap way to sanity-check each revision.

                                            ```ts
                                            const SKILLS_SOURCE = path.resolve(import.meta.dirname,
                                       "../skills");
                                            export function materializeSkills(sandboxDir: string, source:
                                       string = SKILLS_SOURCE): void {
                                              const target = path.join(sandboxDir, ".claude", "skills");
                                              rmSync(target, { recursive: true, force: true });
                                              if (!existsSync(source)) return;
                                              mkdirSync(path.dirname(target), { recursive: true });
                                              cpSync(source, target, { recursive: true });
                                            }
                                            ```
                                            Replace-not-merge so deleted/renamed skills never linger in a
                                       long-lived sandbox.

                                       voice agent: a second intelligence, browser-direct audio, tools

                                       /Users/steve/projects/explore/docs/decisions.md:8:**Decision:**
                                       Realtime voice editing is built on **OpenAI gpt-realtime** (latest
                                       Realtime API version; token supplied by Steve) as a second
                                       intelligence alongside the Claude session — not as a speech front-end
                                       to it. Audio flows **browser ⇄ OpenAI directly over WebRTC** (the
                                       server only mints ephemeral session tokens; the API key never reaches
                                       the browser). Tool calls arrive in the browser on the WebRTC data
                                       channel: front-end tools (screenshot, app state) execute locally;
                                       server tools are forwarded over the existing `/ws` connection as a
                                       `voice:tool` message family, executed server-side against the same
                                       internals the HTTP/MCP surfaces use. The voice model edits directly
                                       (wiki read/search/edit, artifact edits, state writes) **and** can
                                       delegate heavy generation to the Claude session via an
                                       `ask_artifact_agent` tool with two modes — **FAST** and **SMART** —
                                       each selecting an appropriate Claude model for the delegated turn.
                                       The mic button opens a toggled live conversation (VAD + barge-in),
                                       not push-to-talk.
                                       /Users/steve/projects/explore/docs/decisions.md:10:**Persona:** to

2026-07-12 05:47:27  TOOL Skill:       {"skill":"code-clarity"}
2026-07-12 05:47:27  RESULT:           Launching skill: code-clarity
2026-07-12 05:47:27  USER:             Base directory for this skill:
                                       /Users/steve/.claude/skills/code-clarity

                                       # Code Clarity Guidelines [SteveE]

                                       ## Overview

                                       Use this skill as both a standard and an enforcement guide for code
                                       that is easy to read, reason about, review, and safely modify.
                                       Good code keeps the active problem domain small, makes implicit
                                       behavior explicit, keeps reasoning local, and pairs implementation
                                       with tests that prove important behavior.

                                       When acting as the author or owner of the code, update the code so it
                                       follows the standard.
                                       When acting as a reviewer of code you do not own, review the code and
                                       report where it does not follow the standard.

                                       ## Core Principles

                                       - **Review problem state, not syntax.** The more active states,
                                       branches, invariants, pending side effects, and partially transformed
                                       values a piece of code has, the larger the problem domain becomes. A
                                       larger problem domain increases the chance of mistakes when the code
                                       is written, read, reviewed, or modified.

                                       - **Make implicit proof explicit.** Deep access, chained calls,
                                       compact destructuring, optional values, marker states, and object
                                       decomposition all imply facts have been established. If types or
                                       validation do not make that proof obvious, expose it with clearer
                                       structure, naming, validation, assertions, or comments.

                                       - **Preserve meaningful packaging.** Cohesive objects often carry
                                       guarantees that loose fields do not. Avoid decomposing them into
                                       unrelated parameters when the callee needs the packaged meaning, but
                                       avoid passing a large dependency when a smaller meaningful type is
                                       enough.

                                       - **Make active state clear.** In longer methods, it should be
                                       obvious which values are still in play. If a parameter is decomposed
                                       into validated or normalized parts, prefer using those parts
                                       afterward rather than mixing them with the original state.

                                       - **Eliminate cases explicitly.** Early returns, validations,
                                       assertions, exceptions, type narrowing, and guard clauses reduce
                                       later complexity by removing states from consideration. Later code
                                       should be able to rely on the narrower state.

                                       - **Keep process flow clear.** Higher-level process code should read
                                       as a sequence of meaningful operations. Push subtle variant handling,
                                       data mutation, and edge-case work into well-named helpers or domain
                                       operations when that makes the main flow easier to follow.

                                       - **Make causal structure visible.** A reader should be able to see
                                       which facts establish later facts: validation before reliance,
                                       contract before caller assumption, state transition before downstream
                                       use, and root domain decision before derived behavior. If the
                                       dependency chain has to be reconstructed across scattered names,
                                       branches, or helpers, the code still has high reasoning cost.

                                       - **Make state transitions auditable.** When code moves domain state
                                       across phases, revisions, windows, persisted records, or external
                                       boundaries, name the artifact that carries the state, the operation
                                       that consumes it, and the successor state it creates. Prefer a
                                       visible sequence of domain operations over compact control flow when
                                       ordering is part of correctness.

                                       - **Reason about code and tests together.** Tests are dynamic proof.
                                       Production code and tests should form a bonded pair: the code shows
                                       the implementation path, and tests show the behavior space it
                                       survives, including failure modes and uncommon-but-valid states.

                                       - **Prefer stronger correctness mechanisms.** Static guarantees such
                                       as types, schemas, enums, constrained data, and narrow interfaces are
                                       strongest. Runtime validation, assertions, intentional comments, and
                                       tests add proof when static structure cannot express the full
                                       behavior.

                                       - **Use comments for block intent.** Simple statements may be
                                       self-documenting; meaningful blocks often are not. Separate code into
                                       logical parts with short intent comments that explain why the block
                                       exists and what state it establishes.

                                       - **Balance specific and general.** Avoid premature abstraction and
                                       premature specificity. Let names, helpers, and intent describe the
                                       current role clearly, then generalize only when multiple cases reveal
                                       a stable shared shape.

                                       - **Keep domain vocabulary stable.** Names, comments, tests, and
                                       reviewer-facing structure should use the same terms for the same
                                       concepts. A change that introduces new terms, renames domain
                                       concepts, or shifts vocabulary should make the new meaning clear
                                       where it is first used; otherwise readers have to translate between
                                       old and new concepts while reviewing behavior.

                                       - **Make abstractions delete reasoning.** A helper, type, wrapper, or
                                       module boundary earns its place only when it removes active state,
                                       collapses repeated branches, preserves a meaningful domain guarantee,
                                       or gives a stable name to a real concept. If it merely moves the same
                                       reasoning somewhere else, prefer the direct flow.

                                       - **Make absent branches legible.** When a state is unsupported,
                                       impossible, already normalized, or owned by another contract, the
                                       code should make that invariant visible through types, validation,
                                       assertions, narrow interfaces, semantic names, or comments. Do not
                                       leave readers guessing whether an unrepresented state is intentional
                                       or forgotten.

                                       - **Use ordinary good style in service of comprehension.** Prefer
                                       clear names, local conventions, reusable helpers after real patterns
                                       emerge, straightforward code over clever compression, narrow failure
                                       boundaries, explicit inputs and outputs over hidden state, and no
                                       broad style rewrites against coherent existing code.

                                       ## Acting As Author

                                       When you own the change, make the smallest code, test, naming,
                                       validation, helper, or structure update needed to satisfy the
                                       standard.
                                       Preserve behavior unless the user explicitly asks for a behavior
                                       change.
                                       Do not add broad cleanup, formatting churn, speculative abstraction,
                                       or style rewrites outside the touched change.

                                       ## Acting As Reviewer

                                       Use this mode when reviewing code you do not own, when the user asks
                                       for a review, or when direct edits would be inappropriate.

                                       Lead with concrete issues, ordered by severity and grounded in file
                                       and line references when available.
                                       Flag places where code increases reasoning cost: too much active
                                       problem state, unclear proof of validity, lost object guarantees,
                                       unclear marker states, branch-heavy orchestration, broad failure
                                       boundaries, hidden state, premature abstraction, premature
                                       specificity, or tests that do not prove important behavior.
                                       Hypothesize failure cases and uncommon-but-valid values, not just
                                       happy paths.
                                       When a finding involves an abstraction, describe what reasoning it
                                       removes or fails to remove.
                                       When a finding involves an absent branch or unsupported state,
                                       describe what current invariant should make that absence obvious.
                                       When a finding involves vocabulary drift, name the old and new terms
                                       and explain what concept boundary became unclear.
                                       When a finding involves tests, describe the dynamic proof that is
                                       missing rather than only asking for more coverage.

                                       If there are no issues, say that the newly introduced code follows
                                       code comprehension style and name any remaining scope limits.
