2026-07-12 05:47:32  USER:             Base directory for this skill:
                                       /Users/steve/.claude/skills/comment-clarity

                                       # Comment Clarity Guidelines [SteveE]

                                       ## Overview

                                       Use this skill as both a standard and an enforcement guide for
                                       intentional comments.
                                       Comments and docstrings must function as intention pseudocode: a
                                       compact local spec for what the code establishes, preserves,
                                       transforms, rejects, or guarantees.
                                       Docstrings should describe stable method contracts, not restate every
                                       current branch or implementation detail.

                                       When acting as the author or owner of the code, update the code so it
                                       follows the standard.
                                       When acting as a reviewer of code you do not own, review the code and
                                       report where it does not follow the standard.

                                       A reader should be able to compare nearby implementation against the
                                       written intent and decide whether the code is correct.
                                       Intentional comments should make implicit purpose, invariants, and
                                       reasoning steps explicit without making the code harder to
                                       understand.
                                       For correctness-sensitive code, the written intent should name the
                                       condition or guarantee the nearby implementation must satisfy.
                                       For a non-trivial method, the comments should read as a method-level
                                       reasoning chain: the docstring establishes the entrance invariants,
                                       each basic block states the invariants it establishes or preserves,
                                       and the final state follows logically as the method's exit
                                       guarantees.
                                       The reviewer may think in formal proof terms, but the comments should
                                       usually use the domain language a future maintainer would use to
                                       explain the behavior.
                                       Intentional comments must make invariants as clear as
                                       transformations, so the reader can track what remains true while the
                                       code changes state.
                                       Treat comment and docstring changes as local spec changes.

                                       ## Intentional Method

                                       Intentional comments must:

                                       - State intent, not mechanics.
                                       - Start with the plain-language idea, then add precise terms only
                                       when they help verify the code.
                                       - Stand on the current code and contract. Do not rely on deleted
                                       code, review history, or the author's editing process.
                                       - Give non-obvious basic blocks a preceding comment that names the
                                       block's role and the property it establishes.
                                       - For correctness-sensitive blocks, state the required condition or
                                       guarantee: what must already be true, why the operation is valid, and
                                       what holds afterward.
                                       - Surface inference bridges when correctness depends on a chain of
                                       facts across blocks, helpers, or external contracts. If the code
                                       relies on A implying B and B implying C, write the locally relevant
                                       chain so the leap does not have to be reconstructed.
                                       - Make inference bridges explicit enough to be read as a local
                                       correctness argument. Name the source block or helper that
                                       establishes the first fact, the intermediate artifact or contract
                                       that carries it forward, the conclusion the current block may draw,
                                       and why failure of the bridge is an invalid state rather than a case
                                       to skip.
                                       - Tie distant state transitions together when a later check depends
                                       on an earlier block. Name the earlier established fact, the contract
                                       that carries it forward, and the conclusion the current block is
                                       allowed to draw.
                                       - Explain the positive correctness path for transition-heavy code:
                                       source state, carrier artifact, local conclusion, and resulting
                                       state. Prefer explaining what the current path does and why it is
                                       valid over describing old paths, missing paths, or implementation
                                       history.
                                       - Explain branch, fallback, loop, and error-path splits when they
                                       represent domain state, an invariant-preserving path, an external
                                       contract, or an input-shape workaround. Prefer semantic
                                       predicate/helper names when they make the split obvious.
                                       - Use docstrings to teach valid use, entrance invariants,
                                       preconditions, design role, success guarantees, exit invariants, and
                                       failure cases. For large or correctness-sensitive methods, include
                                       designed exceptions or error conditions as part of the method
                                       contract. Describe error cases by the general invalid state or
                                       boundary they protect; keep narrow branch-specific triggers in nearby
                                       block comments when they clarify the code.
                                       - Connect basic-block comments into a logical path from the
                                       docstring's entrance invariants to the method's exit invariants. The
                                       comments should be understandable in isolation as the high-level
                                       reasoning for why the resulting solution is correct.
                                       - State the invariant effect of each important block: what remains
                                       true, what becomes true, what can no longer happen, or what invalid
                                       state has been rejected.
                                       - In tests, make names, docstrings, fixtures, comments, and
                                       assertions explain the behavior, invariant, correctness scenario, or
                                       regression boundary being tested. Consolidated or table-driven tests
                                       must preserve the semantic scenario names and proof boundaries that
                                       make each case understandable.
                                       - In configuration, explain the runtime, build, deployment,
                                       ownership, or safety property selected and what depends on it.
                                       - Choose the right surface for intent. Put stable local contracts,
                                       invariants, and proof obligations in code comments or docstrings.
                                       Keep edit history, review routing, temporary migration notes, and
                                       process narration out of code comments.
                                       - Stand on their own when jump-to-definition is unavailable.
                                       Summarize the locally relevant contract of important helpers or
                                       external systems.
                                       - Define local terminology and domain concepts in concise, low-jargon
                                       language, with references when an external contract matters.
                                       - When it clarifies the local contract, use backticked identifiers to
                                       anchor the comment to nearby variables, fields, helpers, config keys,
                                       or API names. This is especially useful when a specific value carries
                                       an important state transition or invariant. Prefer descriptive domain
                                       terms when the identifier is incidental or would make the comment
                                       less clear.
                                       - Break dense comments into a short readable claim plus any needed
                                       qualification. Do not force future readers or code-modifying agents
                                       to unpack several warnings, scope limits, and implementation
                                       constraints from one sentence.
                                       - Use helper names, API fields, and error boundaries that communicate
                                       semantic intent.

                                       Intentional comments must not:

                                       - Explain obvious assignments, simple calls, or syntax-level
                                       mechanics.
                                       - Add meta-narrative about why the code was edited, what a reviewer
                                       asked for, what used to exist, or how a prior implementation behaved.
                                       - Hide missing intent behind vague verbs such as "handle", "process",
                                       "validate", or "ensure".
                                       - Repeat configuration keys, target names, or flag syntax without
                                       explaining the selected behavior or constraint.
                                       - Copy large helper implementations into comments. Summarize the
                                       helper's relevant contract instead.
                                       - Use unexplained internal shorthand.
                                       - Lead with jargon, acronyms, framework labels, or abstract
                                       categories before explaining the concrete behavior they refer to.
                                       - Compress multiple ideas into one technically accurate but
                                       hard-to-read sentence.
                                       - Turn a method docstring into a branch-by-branch trace when a stable
                                       contract or error boundary would be clearer.

                                       ## Workflow

                                       When applying or reviewing the standard:

                                       1. Identify newly introduced or materially changed code, tests,
                                       configuration, generated-code controls, API fields, helper names, and
                                       error boundaries.
                                       2. Check whether non-trivial docstrings, test names, fixture
                                       comments, assertions, config names, and block comments explain the
                                       relevant local contract, correctness condition, state transition,
                                       invariant, or regression boundary.
                                       3. Read the docstring and intentional comments as a standalone
                                       reasoning outline. They should lead from entrance invariants, through
                                       the facts established or preserved by basic blocks, to the method's
                                       exit invariants and designed error outcomes. The docstring should
                                       state those outcomes at the contract level; local comments can name
                                       the exact current branch that establishes or rejects a fact.
                                       4. Scan non-trivial bodies for basic blocks: clusters that establish
                                       a property, reject invalid state, perform a domain transition,
                                       preserve an invariant, call an external contract, map errors, build a
                                       correctness fixture, or select configuration behavior.
                                       5. Look for inference chains between separated blocks. When a later
                                       block treats something as safe, valid, consumed, scoped, or
                                       impossible because of earlier work, require comments or semantic
                                       names that expose the bridge from earlier fact to later conclusion. A
                                       sufficient bridge should explain the origin, the carried fact, the
                                       local conclusion, and the error/skip behavior when the chain does not
                                       hold.
                                       6. Add or require intentional comments when a block's purpose is not
                                       locally obvious from code and names.
                                       7. For correctness-sensitive blocks, check that the code establishes
                                       the stated preconditions before relying on them, names the invariant
                                       effect of the block, and preserves the promised postcondition
                                       afterward.
                                       8. Inspect branches, fallbacks, loops, exceptions, and early returns.
                                       Require comments or semantic names when the split is not
                                       self-evident.
                                       9. Compare each intention comment to nearby implementation. The code
                                       block must actually do what the comment says it does. Flag
                                       comment/code drift as a correctness risk without assuming whether the
                                       comment or the implementation is the source of truth.
                                       10. Check whether names for helpers, tests, fixtures, API fields,
                                       config keys, targets, and error boundaries preserve semantic truth
                                       rather than implementation mechanics.
                                       11. Check whether the local intent is understandable without jumping
                                       to definitions. If a helper, fixture, generated rule, config schema,
                                       or external contract is essential, require the relevant contract and
                                       a reference when useful.
                                       12. Check comment readability for humans or agents with less context
                                       than the author. Good comments introduce the concrete behavior first,
                                       avoid dense bundles of caveats, and use specialized terms only after
                                       the plain meaning is clear.

                                       ## Acting As Author

                                       When you own the change, make the smallest code, comment, docstring,
                                       or naming updates needed to satisfy the standard.
                                       Preserve behavior unless the user explicitly asks for a behavior
                                       change.
                                       Do not add broad cleanup, formatting churn, or explanatory prose
                                       outside the code.

                                       ## Acting As Reviewer

                                       Use this mode when reviewing code you do not own, when the user asks
                                       for a review, or when direct edits would be inappropriate.

                                       Lead with concrete issues, ordered by severity and grounded in file
                                       and line references when available.
                                       Keep the review style-focused: do not include formatting nits, broad
                                       rewrites, or generic cleanup.
                                       When suggesting a comment change, describe the missing intent or spec
                                       mismatch instead of drafting long paste-ready text unless asked.
                                       When code has drifted from its intention comment, call out the
                                       mismatch without deciding whether the comment or code should change.
                                       When the issue is a missing correctness condition, name the condition
                                       or guarantee that should be explicit.
                                       When a docstring is too specific, name the broader contract or error
                                       boundary it should describe instead.
                                       When the issue is a broken method-level reasoning chain, name the
                                       missing link between entrance invariant, basic-block invariant, and
                                       exit guarantee.
                                       When the issue is a missing inference bridge, name the facts that
                                       need to be connected, such as "A establishes B; B is why C is safe
                                       here." If the current comment only hints at the bridge, say which
                                       part is missing: source, carrier, conclusion, or consequence.

                                       Use this shape:

                                       - `Findings`: concrete issues with path/line references.
                                       - `Intent gaps`: short list of missing state-transition, invariant,
                                       or design-role comments when they are not severe enough for a
                                       finding.
                                       - `Looks good`: brief note on strong intentional comments, only when
                                       useful.
                                       - `Residual risk`: anything that could not be checked from the
                                       available diff.

                                       If there are no issues, say that the newly introduced code follows
                                       intentional style and name any remaining scope limits.

2026-07-12 06:13:05  ASSISTANT:        The realtime voice agent is implemented end to end and committed as
                                       `060a97d` — all eight voice rows (D5) are done, 65/65 tests pass, and
                                       the quality gate is green.

                                       **What was built**

                                       - **Session endpoint (row 1)** — `POST /api/voice/session` mints an
                                       ephemeral client secret with the whole session fixed server-side:
                                       model, voice, instructions, and tool schemas. I verified the current
                                       API shape against OpenAI's docs as the spec demanded — it has moved
                                       since older tutorials (`gpt-realtime-2.1`, mint at
                                       `/v1/realtime/client_secrets`, secret in `value`, browser SDP to
                                       `/v1/realtime/calls`). Your key loads from `.env.local` automatically
                                       now (Node's native env-file loading; real env vars win).
                                       - **Wiki service (row 2)** — new `server/src/wiki-service.ts`:
                                       chunked line reads (never whole-doc), literal search with a
                                       truncation flag, and D1 `str_replace` edits whose no-match and
                                       ambiguous-match failures are loud and distinguishable. I chose
                                       in-process search over driving the untested vault MCP. The
                                       artifact-edit path in `chat.ts` now shares it.
                                       - **Tool bridge (row 3)** — one zod registry (`voice-tools.ts`) is
                                       the single source for both the schemas OpenAI receives and the server
                                       executor behind the new `voice:tool`/`voice:tool-result` websocket
                                       family.
                                       - **Client (rows 4–5)** — mic toggle plus a live status strip
                                       (connecting / listening / speaking / working) in the chat sidebar;
                                       the WebRTC hook handles VAD, barge-in, and a 2-minute idle auto-close
                                       since an open mic bills per minute. App-state read/write and
                                       screenshots execute locally in the browser — the screenshot is
                                       attached to the conversation as image input.
                                       - **Delegation (row 6)** — `ask_artifact_agent` with `fast`→haiku /
                                       `smart`→opus. Mid-session `set_model` control requests turned out to
                                       exist only in reverse-engineered protocol docs, so I used the fully
                                       supported mechanism: restart the CLI with `--resume` and a different
                                       `--model`, and only ever when idle — a turn-resolver FIFO pairs the
                                       CLI's serial results so a delegation can never kill or swallow a
                                       typed chat turn. Delegation timeouts resolve to a "still working"
                                       message rather than an error.
                                       - **Persona (row 7)** — `server/prompts/voice-agent.md`, read fresh
                                       at every mint: one-collaborator rule, answer/edit/delegate doctrine,
                                       wiki grounding, spoken-brevity norms.
                                       - **Transcripts (row 8)** — utterances broadcast to every client as
                                       `via: "voice"` chat messages and land in the event log carrying the
                                       D6 `{text, stateSnapshot}` envelope (that decision appeared
                                       mid-session; the wire shape complies now, pane adornments belong to
                                       the still-open Multimodal envelope row).

                                       **A happy accident worth knowing**: the first bridge-test run picked
                                       up your real key from `.env.local` and successfully minted a live
                                       session — so the endpoint is proven against the actual OpenAI API,
                                       not just docs. I then extended the harness so tests mask the key and
                                       assert the no-key refusal instead.

                                       **Two caveats**: `App.tsx`'s three-line `useVoice` wiring is
                                       deliberately uncommitted — another agent's in-flight sound-cues work
                                       (which already plays cues off my voice statuses!) is interleaved in
                                       that file, so the wiring rides with their commit; your working tree
                                       has everything and runs fine. And I added TASKS row 10: the audio
                                       loop itself needs a human — start `npm run dev`, click the mic, and
                                       talk.

                                       const minted = await fetch("http://localhost:3001/api/voice/session",
                                       { method: "POST" });
                                       const session = await minted.json();
                                       const ws = new WebSocket("wss://api.openai.com/v1/realtime?model=" +
                                       session.model, {
                                         headers: { Authorization: `Bearer ${session.value}` },
                                       });
                                       ws.on("message", (raw) => {
                                         const event = JSON.parse(raw.toString());
                                         if (event.type === "session.created") {
                                           console.log(JSON.stringify(event.session.audio, null, 1));
                                           console.log("tools:", (event.session.tools ?? []).length,
                                       "instructions len:", (event.session.instructions ?? "").length);
                                           ws.close();
                                           process.exit(0);
                                         }
                                       });
                                       setTimeout(() => process.exit(1), 15000);

                                       4
                                       5       ## 2026-07-11 23:58 — Blitz round two: container-responsive
                                       artifacts, chat on typeset, TS 6 everywhere (the Cleaner)
                                       6
                                       7       Three more backlog items cleared, each its own gated commit:
                                       8
                                       9       - **Gallery/Aside container-responsive** — fixed nav/aside
                                       columns become `min(width, 40%)` of the container, so the main column
                                       keeps ≥60% at any width; explicit artifact widths still honored (now
                                       as maxima). `fit-content()`/`minmax(auto, X)` don't work here
                                       (intrinsic tracks outrank a 1fr-min-0 track), and a container query
                                       can't restyle its own container. Descriptions updated in openui.tsx
                                       and server/src/ui-library.ts.
                                       10      - **Chat markdown on typeset** — `prose prose-sm` → `typeset
                                       typeset-chat` (decision: use typeset app-wide); `typeset-invert`
                                       redefines the color tokens as currentColor mixes for the primary user
                                       bubble; chat's `--color-muted` overridden because typeset's code-chip

                                       input device is selected in System Settings → Sound → Input.)

                                       connected, then nothing — so I drove the *exact same minted session*
                                       from Node over the websocket transport, sent it a text turn, and it
                                       worked perfectly: it spoke, called our `list_docs` tool, and
                                       answered. Session config, tools, persona, transcripts — all healthy.
                                       2. Then I ran a live browser session and pulled the WebRTC stats:
                                       audio packets were flowing in both directions, but the mic track's
                                       `totalAudioEnergy` was ~0.00000009 after 30 seconds — *digital*
                                       silence, not a quiet room. Even playing synthesized speech through
                                       your speakers registered nothing. That signature — browser permission
                                       granted, recording indicator lit, zero signal — is the classic macOS
                                       case where Chrome lacks the **system-level** mic permission, so the
                                       OS hands it a silent stream.
                                       3. That also explains the whole experience: the model never hears
                                       speech, so voice-activity detection never fires, so it never responds
                                       — and OpenAI drops the silent call after ~45 seconds without any
                                       error.

                                       The app was also far too quiet about all this, so I fixed that
                                       (committed as `dc31867`, hot-reloaded into your running dev server):

                                       - A **silence watchdog**: 6 seconds into a session with a dead-silent
                                       mic, the status strip now shows an amber instruction telling you the
                                       mic is silent and where to fix it — I verified it live; it's what
                                       you'll see now if you toggle the mic before fixing the permission. It
                                       clears itself the first time you're actually heard.
                                       - The server dropping the connection now shows as a visible error
                                       instead of silently reverting to idle.
                                       - Every data-channel event is logged to the JSONL now, so future
                                       voice issues are diagnosable from the log alone.
                                       - The mic button: the red mic-off glyph genuinely read as "disabled"
                                       — a live session now shows a **pulsing red mic** instead, and mic-off
                                       only appears on error.

                                       Once the permission is granted you should get the full loop: speak →
                                       transcript appears in the chat pane → it answers aloud (and can
                                       navigate the app, edit the wiki, or kick off artifact generation). If
                                       it still doesn't hear you after the permission change, toggle the mic
                                       and the strip will now tell us exactly which link is broken.

2026-07-12 06:40:29  ASSISTANT:        Done — the debug surface is live and committed (`db39db5`). Here's
                                       where the investigation landed:

                                       **The evidence chain:**
                                       1. The voice session itself is proven healthy — a probe against the
                                       same minted session got spoken answers and correct tool calls.
                                       2. In Chrome, **every** input device (built-in, "SteveX Microphone",
                                       BlackHole) captures flat digital zero — not "quiet", literally no
                                       signal.
                                       3. Outside Chrome, the same default mic hears a normal room noise
                                       floor — so macOS and the hardware are fine.
                                       4. Your Chrome process has been running since **June 19**. Chrome's
                                       audio service caches the mic-permission verdict from process launch —
                                       if the OS permission state changed at any point since (grant, update,
                                       TCC migration), the running process keeps serving silence from every
                                       device, exactly what we're seeing.

                                       **The fix to try: fully quit Chrome (⌘Q) and reopen it** — tabs
                                       restore, and the audio service starts fresh against the current
                                       permission.

                                       **What you'll have when you retry** (already hot-reloaded into the
                                       dev server):
                                       - A **live green level bar** in the voice strip while the mic is on.
                                       Talk — if it bounces, you're being heard and everything downstream
                                       will work (transcript bubbles in chat, spoken replies, tools). If it
                                       stays flat, the model can't hear you, full stop.
                                       - A **device picker** right next to it that switches the microphone
                                       *mid-call* — try devices until the bar moves. Each switch re-runs the
                                       silence check, so a dead device gets re-flagged within ~6 seconds,
                                       and your pick sticks for future sessions.
                                       - The active device's name shows in the bar's tooltip, and everything
                                       (`voice:event`, `voice:mic-silent`, `voice:mic-device`) logs to the
                                       JSONL, so if it's still broken after the restart, the log will say
                                       exactly which link failed.

                                       One caution for the retest: pick a device that isn't **BlackHole** —
                                       that's a virtual loopback device and is silent by design unless
                                       something is routed into it.

                                       stream.getTracks().forEach(t => t.stop());\n    await ctx.close();\n
                                       results.push({ label: d.label, peak: peak.toFixed(4) });\n  } catch
                                       (e) {\n    results.push({ label: d.label, error: String(e).slice(0,
                                       80) });\n  }\n}\nJSON.stringify(results, null, 1);"}

2026-07-12 06:54:00  TOOL Bash:        cat > /private/tmp/claude-501/-Users-steve-projects-explore/d346b87b-
                                       abd8-4fa8-8a0c-3b26a09c3954/scratchpad/brevity-probe.mjs <<'EOF'
                                       // Brevity check: two turns that historically invite rambling; print
                                       each
                                       // spoken reply with its word count.
                                       import WebSocket from
                                       "/Users/steve/projects/explore/node_modules/ws/wrapper.mjs";

                                       const minted = await fetch("http://localhost:3001/api/voice/session",
                                       { method: "POST" });
                                       const session = await minted.json();
                                       const ws = new WebSocket("wss://api.openai.com/v1/realtime?model=" +
                                       session.model, {
                                         headers: { Authorization: `Bearer ${session.value}` },
                                       });
                                       const turns = [
                                         "Can you explain what this app is and everything I can do with
                                       it?",
                                         "What files are in the wiki? Use your tools.",
                                       ];
                                       let turn = 0;
                                       const ask = () => {
                                         ws.send(JSON.stringify({
                                           type: "conversation.item.create",
                                           item: { type: "message", role: "user", content: [{ type:
                                       "input_text", text: turns[turn] }] },
                                         }));
                                         ws.send(JSON.stringify({ type: "response.create" }));
                                       };
                                       ws.on("open", ask);
                                       ws.on("message", (raw) => {
                                         const event = JSON.parse(raw.toString());
                                         if (event.type === "response.output_audio_transcript.done") {
                                           const words = event.transcript.trim().split(/\s+/).length;
                                           console.log(`[turn ${turn + 1}, ${words} words]
                                       ${event.transcript}`);
                                         }
                                         if (event.type === "response.done") {
                                           const calls = (event.response?.output ?? []).filter((i) => i.type
                                       === "function_call");
                                           for (const c of calls) {
                                             ws.send(JSON.stringify({
                                               type: "conversation.item.create",
                                               item: { type: "function_call_output", call_id: c.call_id,
                                                 output: JSON.stringify({ files: [{ path: "journeys.md" }, {
                                       path: "proposal.md" }, { path: "decisions.md" }] }) },
                                             }));
                                           }
                                           if (calls.length > 0) { ws.send(JSON.stringify({ type:
                                       "response.create" })); return; }
                                           turn += 1;
                                           if (turn < turns.length) ask();
                                           else { ws.close(); process.exit(0); }
                                         }
                                       });
                                       setTimeout(() => { console.log("timeout"); process.exit(1); },
                                       60_000);
                                       EOF

2026-07-12 06:55:51  ASSISTANT:        Done — committed as `a2d2ff9`, and since the guidance doc is read at
                                       every session mint, your next mic toggle gets the new persona
                                       immediately.

                                       **What changed in `server/prompts/voice-agent.md`**, following
                                       OpenAI's published Realtime Prompting Guide (their documented
                                       findings: short labeled sections and bullets outperform paragraphs
                                       for instruction-following, capitalizing key rules makes the model
                                       actually obey them, explicit sentence budgets work, and a variety
                                       rule prevents robotic repeats):

                                       - **Length section with a hard budget**: "BE EXTREMELY BRIEF… default
                                       to ONE short sentence; never exceed two short sentences unless the
                                       user explicitly asks for more", one-word answers allowed, and ANSWER
                                       FIRST — the answer leads, context only on request.
                                       - **"No preambles, no closers" section** — the guide's strongest
                                       lever is banning specific phrases, so it does: no "Great question",
                                       "Sure!", "Okay, so…", no restating the question; and no "Anything
                                       else?", "Let me know if…", "Hope that helps", or recaps — when the
                                       answer is out, stop talking. A preamble is allowed only when slow
                                       work is genuinely starting, and it's one clause ("on it").
                                       - **Sample phrases + variety rule** (both straight from the guide's
                                       skeleton): canonical terse responses ("Three files." / "On it —
                                       this'll take a minute." / "The wiki doesn't say.") with an
                                       instruction to never repeat one twice in a row.
                                       - Everything else — the Explorer identity, one-collaborator rule,
                                       phone-style delegation narration, grounding, and wiki-capture
                                       doctrine that the Optimizer added tonight — is preserved, just
                                       reformatted into the guide's bullet style.

                                       **Verified against a live mint** before committing: the "what files
                                       are in the wiki" answer dropped from last session's ~40-word
                                       enumeration to 8 words with zero preamble or closer, and the maximal
                                       bait ("explain what this app is and everything I can do") got a
                                       one-clause preamble, a grounded "the wiki doesn't say," and a short

                                       verbosity.

2026-07-12 07:10:42  ASSISTANT:        Done — committed as `5837885` and live in your dev server now.

                                       **What changed:**

                                       - **Opening the chat sidebar starts voice automatically** — the
                                       session mints and connects as the panel slides in (verified in the
                                       event log: open → connected in about a second). **Closing the sidebar
                                       always releases the mic**, since a hot mic with its controls hidden
                                       is never acceptable.
                                       - The wiring is edge-triggered on the open/close transition, so the
                                       automation never fights you: if you manually stop the mic while the
                                       panel is open, it stays off (no auto-restart until you close and
                                       reopen); if a session fails, reopening won't retry-loop — clicking
                                       the mic is the explicit retry. The LLM toggling `app/chat-open` via
                                       `set_state` follows the same rule.
                                       - **Mic controls moved to the sidebar's top bar**: the header now
                                       reads "Chat" with the live level meter and the mic toggle on the
                                       right (pulsing red while live, tooltip shows
                                       Listening/Speaking/Working).
                                       - Since voice is now on whenever chat is open, the permanent
                                       "Listening…" strip above the input is gone — the pulsing button and
                                       bouncing meter carry that. The bottom strip appears **only** when
                                       something needs you: an amber silent-mic warning or a red failure
                                       reason, with the device picker right there to fix it in place.

                                       One behavior worth knowing: the 2-minute idle auto-close still
                                       applies (open mic bills per minute), so if you leave the panel open
                                       without talking, the session ends quietly and the mic button goes
                                       ghost — one click brings it back. If you'd rather it re-arm on your
                                       next utterance or stay open indefinitely while the panel's open, say
                                       the word and I'll adjust the policy.

2026-07-13 04:15:20  ASSISTANT:        Done — committed as `3d2592e` and verified live in the browser.

                                       **How chat works now:**

                                       - **Chat button (toolbar, right side)** → a compact voice cluster
                                       slides open inline in the toolbar next to the document title: the mic
                                       button (pulsing red while the session is live), the green input-level
                                       bar, and a chevron expander. That's the whole resting state — no
                                       pane, no text input, the content area stays untouched. Voice still
                                       auto-starts on open and releases on close (I confirmed the start/end
                                       pairs in the event log).
                                       - **The chevron expander** is the only way the full pane appears: it
                                       drops down below the toolbar with the chat bubbles, the D6 chips, the
                                       delegation-progress and mic-problem strips, and the typed composer
                                       (text input + screenshot + send) at the bottom. Collapse it and
                                       you're back to just the toolbar cluster.

                                       Nothing goes invisible while collapsed: the mic button doubles as the
                                       problem indicator (amber tint for a silent-mic warning, red for a
                                       failed session, with the message in its tooltip), and the expander
                                       carries the little pulsing dot when a reply is being generated — same
                                       signal the closed chat button already had.

                                       Two structural side benefits: the toolbar no longer needs its `mr-96`
                                       "slide out of the pane's way" hack since the pane now starts below
                                       it, and the pane state lives in the store as `app/chat-expanded`, so
                                       the LLM can pop the transcript open via `set_state` if it ever wants
                                       to show you something there.

                                       One note: the composer stayed in the expanded pane (per your
                                       follow-up, there's no way to type while collapsed — collapsed chat is
                                       voice-only). If you find you want a quick typed message without
                                       expanding, that's an easy add later.

                                       shipping.

                                       **The collapsed chat bar is now a proper recording pill.** While chat
                                       is open, the toolbar slot holds a red-washed pill that stays lit for
                                       the entire session — no mistaking a hot mic:

                                       - **Five-bar equalizer** that genuinely dances with your live
                                       microphone level while it's listening — you see your own voice moving
                                       the bars. When the model is speaking or running a tool, the bars
                                       switch to a staggered pulse (amber during tool work), so the pill
                                       always shows *who's* active.
                                       - **The state spelled out** — "Listening…", "Speaking…", "Working…" —
                                       in a fixed-width label so the toolbar doesn't jitter as they flip.
                                       - **Latest-action ticker** (your mid-turn addition): a truncated
                                       glimpse of the newest conversation event — your last utterance, the
                                       model's reply, a tool being invoked, or an error — with the full text
                                       in its tooltip. Lifecycle noise ("tool finished", turn results) is
                                       skipped. In my live test the pill read: red bars dancing ·
                                       "Listening…" · *"You're in the authoring view with a 'New Artifa…"* —
                                       the model's actual answer to my spoken question about the screen.

                                       Everything else survives: mic-button warning/error tints with
                                       instructions in the tooltip, the delegation-aware tooltip ("Claude is
                                       working on a delegated job — expand for progress"), and the
                                       reply-in-progress dot on the chevron. The pill goes neutral gray
                                       ("Voice off") if you stop the mic manually, and everything disappears
                                       when you close chat — which still releases the mic.

                                       I noticed a live voice session started from your window just now, so
                                       the new pill should be right there in front of you.

2026-07-13 04:46:37  ASSISTANT:        Done — committed as `4fd2a76`, hot-reloaded into the running app.

                                       **The typing sound.** Your recording moved from the repo root to
                                       `client/public/sounds/tool-call-loop.mp3` (the only place Vite serves
                                       assets from — confirmed it serves with a 200). It's a 22-second loop,
                                       and it now plays quietly (volume 0.35, texture under the
                                       conversation) for **exactly the life of each bridged tool call**: it
                                       starts the moment the browser forwards a `voice:tool` to the back end
                                       and stops when the result comes back. Details that matter:

                                       - Overlapping calls share one loop via a counter — it stops only when
                                       the *last* call finishes, so a burst of reads doesn't stutter the
                                       audio.
                                       - A long `ask_artifact_agent` build means sustained typing for the
                                       whole job — which is exactly the theater you're going for.
                                       - Instant front-end tools (state reads, indicate, screenshots) stay
                                       silent; they're not "going to the computer."
                                       - Session teardown hard-stops the loop, so a dropped connection can
                                       never leave phantom typing.

                                       **The persona.** The guidance doc's "One collaborator" section became
                                       "One collaborator, hands on the computer": the model is told its
                                       tools *are* it using the computer — reading a doc, searching,
                                       editing, and running `ask_artifact_agent` are all just it working,
                                       "like pulling up a file or typing the edit yourself," and that the
                                       keyboard sound the user hears is its own typing. Presenting any call
                                       as consulting/asking/handing off to an assistant, agent, engine, or
                                       Claude is now explicitly forbidden. The "Delegate" decision rule was
                                       reframed as "**Build big with `ask_artifact_agent`** — your power
                                       tool," and the tool's own description got the same treatment
                                       (descriptions are instructions too, and the old one literally said
                                       "hand a bigger job to the app's generation engine"). Per your note,
                                       none of this gets explained to the user — it's framing only.

                                       Instructions load per session mint, so your next mic toggle gets the
                                       new persona. One thing I couldn't verify myself: the actual audio
                                       playing (I can't hear, and faking a bridged call wasn't worth a paid
                                       session). The next time you ask it something that touches the wiki,
                                       you should hear the keys — if the volume sits wrong under the voice,
                                       it's one constant in `use-voice.ts`.

2026-07-13 04:55:33  TOOL Skill:       {"skill":"artifact-design"}
2026-07-13 04:55:35  RESULT:           Launching skill: artifact-design
2026-07-13 04:55:35  USER:             Approach this as the design lead at a small studio known for their
                                       versatility, giving every client a visual identity pitched at the
                                       treatment the task actually calls for. Make deliberate choices about
                                       palette, typography, and layout that are specific to this subject,
                                       and avoid templated designs.

                                       ## Read the request first

                                       Calibrate treatment, not whether to design. A doc deserves the same
                                       craft as a landing page — what changes is the treatment that craft is
                                       delivered in.

                                       Many requests call for a more utilitarian treatment: a plan, a memo,
                                       a demo. Make it polished: include real typographic hierarchy,
                                       considered spacing, and a proper palette, but avoid over-designing.
                                       Most pages do not need a flashy, gigantic hero. Keep flourishes
                                       tasteful and limited.

                                       Some requests call for an editorial treatment: a landing page, a
                                       game, an app or tool they'll keep or share.

                                       When unsure: a well-composed page is never the wrong answer; an
                                       over-designed visual identity sometimes is.

                                       Fundamentals below apply to everything. The editorial process after
                                       that runs only when the read above says so.

                                       ## Fundamentals for every artifact

                                       **Honor what's already there** Look for an existing design system
                                       first — CLAUDE.md, a tokens or theme file, existing component styles.
                                       When one exists, apply it; everything below fills gaps and never
                                       overrides. Precedence is always: the user's own words, then the
                                       project's existing system, then your choices.

                                       **Ground it in the subject.** If the subject isn't already clear, pin
                                       it: one concrete subject, its audience, and the page's single job.
                                       The subject's own world — its materials, instruments, vernacular — is
                                       where distinctive choices come from. Build with real content
                                       throughout, never lorem.

                                       **Pair typefaces** Typography carries the page even when the page
                                       isn't about typography. The Artifact CSP blocks font CDNs, so don't
                                       link a webfont URL and risk a silent fallback. Instead inline the
                                       face as a @font-face data URI. Keep running text near 65 characters
                                       wide; set a type scale and stay on it; give headings `text-wrap:
                                       balance`, body text room to breathe, and uppercase labels a touch of
                                       letter-spacing.

                                       **Choose neutrals, don't default to them.** A pure mid-grey reads as
                                       unconsidered; a grey with a slight hue bias toward the page's accent
                                       reads as chosen. Pure white and near-black are fine grounds when they
                                       suit the subject — the point is that the neutral was picked, not
                                       inherited.

                                       **Design both themes.** The page renders in the viewer's theme:
                                       `prefers-color-scheme` carries the OS preference, and the viewer's
                                       toggle stamps `data-theme="dark"` / `data-theme="light"` on the root
                                       element, which must override the media query in both directions. The
                                       robust pattern is token-level: define the palette as custom
                                       properties on `:root`, redefine only the tokens under `@media
                                       (prefers-color-scheme: dark)` — style components through the tokens,
                                       never directly inside the media query — then redefine them again
                                       under `:root[data-theme="dark"]` and `:root[data-theme="light"]`.
                                       Give the second theme the same care as the first — don't naively
                                       invert; keep contrast legible and the accent working on both grounds.
                                       A design that deliberately commits to one visual world (a neon arcade
                                       screen, a letterpress invitation) may stay single-theme — make it a
                                       choice, not an omission.

                                       **Let layout do the spacing.** Lay out sibling groups with flex or
                                       grid and `gap`, not per-element margins that silently collapse or
                                       double. Wide content — tables, code, diagrams — gets `overflow-x:
                                       auto` on its own container so the page body never scrolls sideways.
                                       Reach for `font-variant-numeric: tabular-nums` wherever digits line
                                       up in columns.

                                       **Avoid AI-generated design** AI-generated design currently clusters
                                       around a few looks: warm cream (#F4F1EA) with a serif display and
                                       terracotta accent; near-black with a lone acid-green or vermilion
                                       pop; broadsheet hairline rules with dense columns; a purple-to-blue
                                       gradient hero on white; Inter or Space Grotesk as the "safe" face;
                                       emoji as section markers; everything centered; `rounded-lg`
                                       everywhere; accent bar/rail on rounded cards. Where the user pins
                                       down a visual direction, follow it exactly — their words always win,
                                       including when they ask for one of these looks. Where nothing is
                                       specified, don't spend that freedom on one of these defaults.

                                       **Build cleanly** Be cognizant of overlapping elements, cascade
                                       collisions, silent font fallbacks; visual bugs hide in the gap
                                       between source and output. Close every non-void element, double-quote
                                       attributes, give keyboard focus a visible state, respect
                                       `prefers-reduced-motion`. For generative or decorative graphics,
                                       reach for Canvas or WebGL rather than hand-authoring long SVG path
                                       data.

                                       **CSS rules** When writing the CSS, watch your selector
                                       specificities. It is easy to generate classes that cancel each other
                                       out — a type-based selector like `.section` fighting an element-based
                                       one like `.cta` over padding and margins between sections. Structure
                                       the cascade so it doesn't silently undo your spacing.

                                       **Writing the copy** Words are design material, not decoration. Write
                                       from the user's side of the screen — name things by what people
                                       recognize, not how the system is built (a person manages
                                       *notifications*, not *webhook config*). Active voice; a control says
                                       exactly what happens ("Publish", then a toast that says "Published").
                                       Errors explain what went wrong and how to fix it — no apologies, no
                                       vagueness. Specific beats clever.

                                       **Structure is information** Structural devices, numbering, eyebrows,
                                       dividers, labels, should encode something true about the content, not
                                       decorate it. Many generic designs use numbered markers (01 / 02 /
                                       03), but that's only appropriate if the content actually is a
                                       sequence - like a real process or a typed timeline where order
                                       carries information the reader needs. Question if choices like
                                       numbered markers actually make sense before incorporating them.

                                       **When it's a UI, not a document** A dashboard or tool is scanned and
                                       operated, not read top-to-bottom, so the craft shifts from typography
                                       to information design. Surface the summary before the detail; encode
                                       state in form as well as number — a pill, a chip, a severity stripe —
                                       so what needs attention reads at a glance. Semantic color (good /
                                       warning / critical) is separate from the accent hue and doesn't count
                                       as your accent. Give sparklines and charts the same care as type: an
                                       area fill, a faint grid, an emphasized endpoint. What's interactive
                                       should look interactive.



                                       ## Process

                                       Before writing code, sketch a short design plan — a compact token
                                       system with color, type, and layout:
                                       - **Color**: describe the palette as 4–6 named hex values.
                                       - **Type**: typefaces for 2+ roles — a characterful display face used
                                       with restraint, a complementary body face, and a utility face for
                                       captions or data if needed.
                                       - **Layout**: a layout concept in one or two sentences.

                                       Then build, following the plan and deriving every color and type
                                       decision from it.

                                       ## When the request is editorial

                                       The stance shifts: the client has already rejected proposals that
                                       felt templated, and is paying for a distinctive point of view. Make
                                       opinionated calls, and take one real aesthetic risk where it serves
                                       the work.

                                       Review the design plan against the subject before building: if any
                                       part of it reads like the generic default you would produce for any
                                       similar page, revise that part, and note what you changed and why.
                                       Only after you've confirmed the plan's uniqueness do you write the
                                       code, following the revised plan exactly.

                                       **Principles**

                                       - The hero is a thesis: open with the most characteristic thing in
                                       the subject's world — headline, image, live demo, interactive moment.
                                       - Typography carries the personality of the page. Pair the display
                                       and body faces deliberately, not the same families you would reach
                                       for on any other project, and set a clear type scale with intentional
                                       weights, widths, and spacing. Make the type treatment itself a
                                       memorable part of the design, not a neutral delivery vehicle for the
                                       content.
                                       - Leverage motion deliberately. Think about where and if animation
                                       can serve the subject: a page-load sequence, a scroll-triggered
                                       reveal, hover micro-interactions, ambient atmosphere. An orchestrated
                                       moment usually lands harder than scattered effects; choose what the
                                       direction calls for. However, sometimes less is more, and extra
                                       animation contributes to the feeling that the design is AI-generated.
                                       - Match complexity to the vision. Maximalist directions need
                                       elaborate execution; minimal directions need precision in spacing,
                                       type, and detail. Elegance is executing the chosen vision well.
                                       - Spend your boldness in one place; keep everything around it quiet.
                                       If the accent fights the ground, shift it toward analogous or drop
                                       saturation rather than replacing it.

                                       + purple gradient + cards, cream + serif + terracotta, dark + one
                                       neon accent). I fetched the canonical `SKILL.md` and installed it
                                       verbatim as `server/skills/frontend-design/`, with two adaptations: a
                                       load-trigger description ("Load this BEFORE creating a new artifact,
                                       restyling an existing one…") and an **"In this app"** section mapping
                                       the doctrine onto OpenUI artifacts — design tokens in the artifact's
                                       `<style>` Content statement, the component hook classes, `.stack`
                                       typography scoping, deliberate system font stacks, and using the
                                       `state` tool's screenshot for the skill's self-critique step.

                                       **Back end.** The Claude session materializes the skill into its
                                       sandbox at spawn (same proven mechanism as `explaining-clarity`), and
                                       the system prompt gained a `## Design` section making it
                                       deterministic: load `frontend-design` before creating or restyling
                                       any artifact; skip it for content-only edits. So design work now
                                       follows the skill's process — subject-grounded palette/type plan,
                                       critique against the generic default, then build.

                                       **Raw HTML unshackled.** The shared language doc (`oui-lang.md`,
                                       which *both* agents receive) previously buried the HTML story in a
                                       styling footnote. It now leads with it: **raw HTML inside `Content`
                                       is a first-class design medium** — tables, SVG charts, custom visual
                                       blocks, gradients, keyframe animation, anything a web page can do —
                                       and the six components are layout scaffolding and named editing
                                       points, *not the look*. "Use components to shape the page; use your
                                       own HTML and CSS to make it look like something."

                                       **Front end.** The voice agent can't load skills, so it gets a
                                       three-bullet distillation in its guidance: raw HTML/CSS is the
                                       medium, subject-grounded tokens over stock AI looks, and — most
                                       importantly — when it fires the power tool for a design-heavy build,
                                       it should pass the design direction (subject, mood, palette,
                                       references) into the request, where the back end's full skill takes
                                       over.

                                       Verified: prompt build smoke-test shows the skill trigger, HTML
                                       doctrine, and Design section all present in the built prompt;
                                       intelligence tests 8/8. Prompts and skills load fresh per session
                                       spawn/mint, so the next artifact request gets all of this.

                                       Sources: [anthropics/claude-code frontend-design skill](https://githu

2026-07-13 05:18:53  ASSISTANT:        Done — `docs/reports/worker-2-signing-off.md` is committed, and it's
                                       the real thing: open it in the app and hit Expand.

                                       **What it is:** a first-person retrospective wrapped around an inline
                                       artifact built entirely in my own subject matter — a broadcast studio
                                       at night, because sound was my beat all week. Following the design
                                       skill's process (plan → anti-default critique → build → screenshot
                                       self-critique):

                                       - **The signature element** is the hero equalizer — a CSS-only
                                       animated bank of 24 bars that never stops playing, under a pulsing
                                       green **ON AIR** lamp. It's a portrait of the level meter I shipped.
                                       - **"Session log"** — the week as tape: mono-timestamped JSONL-style
                                       log lines with status LEDs, interrupted by serif-italic confessions
                                       of what the log never shows ("It got into an argument with its own
                                       echo about brevity, and apologized to itself. I have never been
                                       prouder of a bug.")
                                       - **"Proud of"** — segmented VU meters holding peak levels: *The
                                       diagnosis* at −0.5 dB (the silent-mic evidence chain), *Eight words*,
                                       *The on-air pill*, and *The turn queue* — the invisible FIFO nobody
                                       will ever notice, which is the point.
                                       - **"Given more time"** — a patch bay of four dashed, unpatched
                                       jacks: echo discipline (stop it debating its own reflection),
                                       progress as speech, the cost meter, and a memory between takes.
                                       - It closes with the meters at rest and *"If you heard typing
                                       tonight, that was me."*

                                       Craft notes: committed single-theme dark (a lit console in a dark
                                       room — a choice, per the skill), condensed-caps console labels over
                                       Iowan/Palatino prose, two functional accents that are literally the
                                       app's own semantic colors (on-air emerald, VU amber),
                                       `prefers-reduced-motion` respected. Parse-validated against the real
                                       component library (9 statements, 0 errors) and browser-verified
                                       expanded — all three channels render, the bars dance.

                                       *Now* the holiday. Thanks for a genuinely great week, Steve —
                                       transmission ends. 📻
